  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16116594341751042776">For over one hundred years, Christians have gotten up and gone to bed with Charles Spurgeon's devotional Morning and Evening as a companion. With a reading to begin and end each day throughout the year, you will come to appreciate Spurgeon's emphasis on the importance of abiding in Christ and meditating on God's Word. His wisdom and counsel provide a timeless guide through</span>
  <span id="freeText16116594341751042776" style="display:none">For over one hundred years, Christians have gotten up and gone to bed with Charles Spurgeon's devotional Morning and Evening as a companion. With a reading to begin and end each day throughout the year, you will come to appreciate Spurgeon's emphasis on the importance of abiding in Christ and meditating on God's Word. His wisdom and counsel provide a timeless guide through the trials and triumphs of the year. The richness of his biblical understanding offers readers a look into the heart of one of England's foremost pastors and enduring Christian authors.<br /><br />His lasting message is even more accessible with Alistair Begg's careful modernizing of Spurgeon's English. Begg, who has a deep love for Spurgeon's preaching and especially for this work, has maintained Spurgeon's clear passion and commitment to Christ. Using the English Standard Version as the scriptural text provides an accurate, understandable accompaniment to Spurgeon's lessons.<br /><br />This updated version of a devotional classic is a timely and much-needed encouragement for today's Christian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16116594341751042776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204855600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2348240130909099737">Truly superb! Spurgeon's language is approachable yet lofty. The daily format is ideal to accomplish a major impact a little at a time on multiple fronts in the reader's life. Spurgeon comes across as insistent on Christ's best for the reader's life but in a jovial, fatherly way that will have the reader looking forward to the next visit.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2649605620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2649605620" />
    <a title="Brian Eshleman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862823-brian-eshleman"><img alt="Brian Eshleman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591296763p2/5862823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2649605620?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Eshleman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Eshleman" href="/user/show/5862823-brian-eshleman">Brian Eshleman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2649605620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16540612222045921432">I've run out of annual superlatives. I'm a guy who doesn't typically reread. I'm a guy who doesn't typically need, he thought, commentaries to chew his spiritual food for him. I'm a guy who tended to think more is more, anyway, when commenting on Scripture. What could a paragraph or two on a sliver of Scripture, injected steadily every day do?<br/><br/>Four or five years later, I'm still finding out. Spurgeon would never settle for any comparison that the splendor of his language is near to that of Script</span>
  <span id="freeText16540612222045921432" style="display:none">I've run out of annual superlatives. I'm a guy who doesn't typically reread. I'm a guy who doesn't typically need, he thought, commentaries to chew his spiritual food for him. I'm a guy who tended to think more is more, anyway, when commenting on Scripture. What could a paragraph or two on a sliver of Scripture, injected steadily every day do?<br /><br />Four or five years later, I'm still finding out. Spurgeon would never settle for any comparison that the splendor of his language is near to that of Scripture, but let's just say his love of Scripture and Scripture's God glows through his own word choices. And as much as he clearly loves the Word itself and weaves it into his entries, Spurgeon's analogies show a man who also sees God's glory, subtle and grand, unbound by any book's pages.<br /><br />He would be the last to center on man's affection or approval. Yet by this very freedom does his shepherding heart comes through. His confrontations are not dulled by the years that have intervened since this book was written. His exhortations still ring clearly. His love for the reader in the current day is as clear as that love for the people who sat under his teaching as he preached.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16540612222045921432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1495924589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1495924589" />
    <a title="MC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164369-mc"><img alt="MC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483779945p2/28164369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1495924589?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MC" href="/user/show/28164369-mc">MC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19013201-morning-evening">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1495924589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13207365794908042041"><i>Morning & Evening</i> is perhaps the seminal book Charles Spurgeon's career. Despite how prolific his writings and statements were, this is what folks think of when it comes to a devotional of his. It's one of the best-loved devotional works ever.<br/><br/>Certainly it's easy to see why. I greatly benefitted from the optimism of Spurgeon. None of the negative stuff that so many have at times espoused. Yes, there is suffering, as Spurgeon well knew, but there is also joy.<br/><br/>If it were not for the values dissonanc</span>
  <span id="freeText13207365794908042041" style="display:none"><i>Morning &amp; Evening</i> is perhaps the seminal book Charles Spurgeon's career. Despite how prolific his writings and statements were, this is what folks think of when it comes to a devotional of his. It's one of the best-loved devotional works ever.<br /><br />Certainly it's easy to see why. I greatly benefitted from the optimism of Spurgeon. None of the negative stuff that so many have at times espoused. Yes, there is suffering, as Spurgeon well knew, but there is also joy.<br /><br />If it were not for the values dissonance (not in terms of morality but in terms of certain activities like recreation being bad or what not) this book would have been near perfect. Great book and I really recommend it.<br /><br />Rating 3.5 Stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13207365794908042041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2643441512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643441512" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643441512?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13381226-morning-and-evening">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=operationactuallybooks">operationactuallybooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2018goodrule-old">2018goodrule-old</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2018reviews">2018reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643441512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13060017180012873148">Morning and Evening is a classic devotional by Charles H. Spurgeon that was originally published in 1866.<br/><br/>There is a devotional for every morning and every evening.<br/><br/>Each devotional begins with a bite-sized portion of Scripture.<br/><br/>Spurgeon "feeds" his flock from both the Old Testament and the New Testament.<br/><br/>He speaks directly to readers and addresses matters of great importance. His works are ever-relevant.<br/><br/>I've been sharing quotes from Morning and Evening since the first week of January when I began re</span>
  <span id="freeText13060017180012873148" style="display:none">Morning and Evening is a classic devotional by Charles H. Spurgeon that was originally published in 1866.<br /><br />There is a devotional for every morning and every evening.<br /><br />Each devotional begins with a bite-sized portion of Scripture.<br /><br />Spurgeon "feeds" his flock from both the Old Testament and the New Testament.<br /><br />He speaks directly to readers and addresses matters of great importance. His works are ever-relevant.<br /><br />I've been sharing quotes from Morning and Evening since the first week of January when I began reading the devotional.<br /><br />I'll share my top twenty or so with you now.<br /><br />From December:<br /><br />The night of affliction is as much under the arrangement and control of the Lord of Love—as the bright summer days when all is bliss. Jesus is in the tempest! His love wraps the night as a cloak—but to the eye of faith the sable robe is scarcely a disguise.<br />His presence will be most realized—by those who are most like Him. If you desire to see Christ, you must grow in conformity to Him.<br />Christian, God has not left you in your earthly pilgrimage to an angel’s guidance—He Himself leads the van. You may not see the cloudy, fiery pillar—but Jehovah will never forsake you.<br />Christ is the great Peacemaker; but before peace, He brings war. Where the light comes, the darkness must retire. Where truth is, the lie must flee; or, if it abides, there must be a stern conflict, for the truth cannot and will not lower its standard, and the lie must be trodden under foot.<br /><br />From November:<br />The past is gone; the future has not arrived; we never shall have any time but time present. Then do not fritter away your life in thinking of what you intend to do tomorrow, as if that could recompense for the idleness of today. No man ever served God by doing things tomorrow.<br />Truth must enter into the soul, penetrate and saturate it—or else it is of no value. Doctrines held as a matter of mere creed—are like bread in the hand, which ministers no nourishment to the body.<br />Be content with such things as you have, since the Lord has ordered all things for your good. Take up your own daily cross; it is the burden best suited for your shoulder, and will prove most effective to make you perfect in every good word and work to the glory of God.<br />To have one foot on the land of truth, and another on the sea of falsehood, will end in a terrible fall and a total ruin. Christ will be all—or nothing.<br />From October:<br />“I will love them freely.” Hosea 14:4 This sentence is a body of divinity in miniature. He who understands its meaning, is a theologian; and he who can dive into its fullness, is a true spiritual master. It is a summary of the glorious message of salvation, which was delivered to us in Christ Jesus our Redeemer. The meaning hinges upon the word “freely.” This is the glorious, the suitable, the divine way by which love streams from heaven to earth—a spontaneous love flowing forth to those who neither deserved it, purchased it, nor sought after it. It is, indeed, the only way in which God can love such as we are. The text is a death-blow to all sorts of fitness, “I will love them freely.”<br />We ought to muse upon the things of God, because we thus get the real nutriment out of them. Hearing, reading, and learning—all require inward digesting to complete their usefulness, and the inward digesting of the truth lies for the most part in meditating upon it.<br />When we repent of sin, we must have one eye upon SIN—and another upon the CROSS! It will be better still—if we fix both our eyes upon Christ—and see our transgressions only in the light of His love.<br />Each believer must, when filled with a sense of Jesus’ love—be also overwhelmed with astonishment, that such divine love should be lavished on an object so utterly unworthy of it. Jesus must have found the cause of His love—in His own heart. He could not have found it in us—for it is not there! <br />From September:<br />Wherever Jesus may lead us—He goes before us. If we know not where we go, we know with whom we go. With such a companion, who will dread the perils of the road? The journey may be long—but His everlasting arms will carry us to the end.<br />Scripture is a never-failing treasury filled with boundless stores of grace. It is the bank of heaven; you may draw from it as much as you please, without price or hindrance. Come in faith and you are welcome to all covenant blessings. There is not a promise in the Word which shall be withheld.<br />A Christian man should so shine in his life, that a person could not live with him a week, without knowing the gospel. His conversation should be such that all who are about him should clearly perceive whose he is, and whom he serves; and should see the image of Jesus reflected in his daily actions.<br />From August:<br />My Lord is more ready to pardon—than you to sin; more able to forgive—than you to transgress. My Master is more willing to supply your needs—than you are to ask for them!<br />Do you dread sin? He has nailed it to His cross! Do you fear death? He has been the death of death! Are you afraid of hell? He has barred it against the entrance of any of His children; they shall never see the gulf of perdition!<br />Let a Christian begin to boast, “I can do all things,” without adding “through Christ who strengthens me,” and before long he will have to groan, “I can do nothing,” and bemoan himself in the dust. When we do anything for the Lord, and He is pleased to accept of our doings, let us lay our crown at His feet, and exclaim, “Not I—but the grace of God which was with me!”<br />From July:<br />It is impossible for any human speech to express the full meaning of this delightful phrase, “God is for me.” He was “for us” before the worlds were made. He was “for us,” or He would not have given His well-beloved son. He was “for us” when He smote the Only-begotten, and laid the full weight of His wrath upon Him—He was “for us,” though He was against Him. He was “for us,” when we were ruined in the fall—He loved us notwithstanding all. He was “for us,” when we were rebels against Him, and with a high hand were bidding Him defiance. He was “for us,” or He would not have brought us humbly to seek His face. He has been “for us” in many struggles; we have been summoned to encounter hosts of dangers; we have been assailed by temptations from without and within—how could we have remained unharmed to this hour—if He had not been “for us”? He is “for us,” with all the infinity of His being; with all the omnipotence of His love; with all the infallibility of His wisdom; arrayed in all His divine attributes, He is “for us,” eternally and immutably “for us”; “for us” when yon blue skies shall be rolled up like a worn out vesture; “for us” throughout eternity!<br />Blessed is the fact that Christians can rejoice even in the deepest distress; although trouble may surround them, they still sing; and, like many birds, they sing best in their cages. Trouble does not necessarily bring consolation with it to the believer—but the presence of the Son of God in the fiery furnace with him fills his heart with joy. He is sick and suffering—but Jesus visits him and makes his bed for him. He is dying, and the cold chilly waters of Jordan are gathering about him up to the neck—but Jesus puts His arms around him, and cries, “Fear not, beloved!<br />From June:<br />“Help, Lord!” will suit us living and dying, suffering or laboring, rejoicing or sorrowing.<br />After conversion our God is our joy, comfort, guide, teacher, and in every sense our light—He is light within, light around, light reflected from us, and light to be revealed to us.<br />If you are not humbled in the presence of Jesus—you do not know Him. You were so lost that nothing could save you—but the sacrifice of God’s only begotten Son. Think of that, and as Jesus stooped for you—bow yourself in lowliness at His feet.<br />The Scriptures reveal Jesus, “The Scriptures point to Me!” No more powerful motive can be urged upon Bible readers than this—he who finds Jesus finds life, heaven, all things. Happy he who, searching his Bible, discovers his Savior!<br />From May:<br />There is no need for God to create a new thing upon the earth in order to restore believers to joy; if they would prayerfully rake the ashes of the past, they would find light for the present; and if they would turn to the book of truth and the throne of grace, their candle would soon shine as aforetime.<br />Christian, what have you to do with sin? Has it not cost you enough already? Burnt child—will you play with the fire? What! when you have already been between the jaws of the lion—will you step a second time into his den? Have you not had enough of the old serpent? Did he not poison all your veins once—and will you play upon the hole of the viper, and put your hand upon the cockatrice’s den a second time? Did sin ever yield you real pleasure? Did you find solid satisfaction in it? If so, go back to your old drudgery, and wear the chain again—if it delights you. But inasmuch as sin did never give you what it promised to bestow—but deluded you with lies—do not be snared a second time by the old fowler!<br />What a comfort to know that we have a great Physician who is both able and willing to heal us! Let us think of Him for a while tonight. His cures are very speedy—there is life in a look at Him. His cures are radical—He strikes at the center of the disease. And hence, His cures are sure and certain. He never fails, and the disease never returns. There is no relapse where Christ heals—there is no fear that His patients should be merely patched up for a season. He is well skilled in all diseases. Jesus Christ is thoroughly acquainted with the whole of human nature. He is as much at home with one sinner as with another, and never yet did He meet with an unusual case which was difficult to Him.<br />Oh, do not think, believer, that your sorrows are out of God’s plan; they are necessary parts of it.<br />The gospel is a very bold gospel, it fearlessly proclaims the truth, whether men like it or not. We must be equally faithful and unflinching.<br />From April:<br />Banquet your faith upon God’s own Word, and whatever your fears or needs, repair to the Bank of Faith with your Father’s hand-written note, saying, “Remember the Word unto Your servant—upon which You have caused me to hope.”<br /><br />Let us fight as if it all depended upon us—but let us look up and know that all depends upon Him!<br />We are not far from home—a moment will bring us there.<br />Remember that the same Christ who tells us to say, “Give us this day our daily bread,” had first given us this petition, “Hallowed be Your name; Your kingdom come; Your will be done in earth as it is in heaven.” Let not your prayers be all concerning your own sins, your own needs, your own imperfections, your own trials—but let them climb the starry ladder, and get up to Christ Himself, and then, as you draw near to the blood-sprinkled mercy-seat, offer this prayer continually, “Lord, extend the kingdom of Your dear Son!” Such a petition, fervently presented, will elevate the spirit of all your devotions. Mind that you prove the sincerity of your prayer by laboring to promote the Lord’s glory.<br /><br />From March:<br />Great thoughts of your sin alone—will drive you to despair; but great thoughts of Christ—will pilot you into the haven of peace. “My sins are many—but oh! it is nothing to Jesus to take them all away. The weight of my guilt presses me down as a giant’s foot would crush a worm—but it is no more than a grain of dust to Him, because He has already borne its curse on the cruel tree. It will be but a small thing for Him to give me full remission, although it will be an infinite blessing for me to receive.<br />There is no road between my soul and heaven—but faith.<br />Look upon all sin as that which crucified your Savior—and you will see it to be “exceeding sinful.”<br />From February:<br />“He has said” must be our daily resort.<br />We would be abler teachers of others, and less liable to be carried about by every wind of doctrine—if we sought to have a more intelligent understanding of the Word of God. As the Holy Spirit, the Author of the Scriptures is He who alone can enlighten us rightly to understand them, we should constantly ask His teaching, and His guidance into all truth.<br />A daily portion is all that a man really needs. We do not need tomorrow’s supplies; for that day has not yet dawned, and its needs are as yet unborn. The thirst which we may suffer in the month of June—does not need to be quenched in February, for we do not feel it yet.<br />Christian, meditate much on heaven—it will help you to press on, and to forget the toil of the way. This valley of tears is but the pathway to the better country! This present world of woe is but the stepping-stone to a world of bliss.<br />From January:<br />We must not cease to wonder at the great marvels of our God. It would be very difficult to draw a line between holy wonder—and real worship; for when the soul is overwhelmed with the majesty of God’s glory, though it may not express itself in song, or even utter its voice with bowed head in humble prayer—yet it silently adores.<br />Christ is not only “mighty to save” those who repent—but He is able to make men repent. He will carry those who believe those to heaven; but He is, moreover, mighty to give men new hearts and to work faith in them. He is mighty to make the man who hates holiness—love it; and to constrain the despiser of His name—to bend the knee before Him.<br />How different will be the state of the believer in heaven—from what it is here! Here he is born to toil and suffer weariness—but in the land of the immortal, fatigue is never known.<br />He who does not grow in the knowledge of Jesus, refuses to be blessed. To know Him is “life eternal,” and to advance in the knowledge of Him is to increase in happiness. He who does not long to know more of Christ—knows nothing of Him yet.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13060017180012873148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1514656853?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/51647109-cathy">Cathy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6588025-morning-and-evening">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=sermons">sermons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=shelfari-favorites">shelfari-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=faith">faith</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=hope">hope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=beautiful-word-pictures">beautiful-word-pictures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=comfort">comfort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=devotions">devotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=forgiveness">forgiveness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51647109-cathy?shelf=good-shepherd">good-shepherd</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514656853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer574820304071375935">I find myself sad to have finished this book, and wish that there was more of it. I had set it up to pop up on my computer, whenever I logged in, and often, it was the most encouraging "email" of my day. I have found Spurgeon's writings to be so comforting, encouraging, and challenging at times, perfect for this season of my life. He doesn't shy away from the tough aspects of life, but he doesn't delve into the technical details of a verse as many of today's pastors do. He compares them to heart</span>
  <span id="freeText574820304071375935" style="display:none">I find myself sad to have finished this book, and wish that there was more of it. I had set it up to pop up on my computer, whenever I logged in, and often, it was the most encouraging "email" of my day. I have found Spurgeon's writings to be so comforting, encouraging, and challenging at times, perfect for this season of my life. He doesn't shy away from the tough aspects of life, but he doesn't delve into the technical details of a verse as many of today's pastors do. He compares them to heart issues. Some of these, I have sent friends to encourage them. You do have to be comfortable with old English to enjoy these. My favorites include: The Voice of Weeping shall no more be heard, Into Thine Hand I commit my spirit, Satan Hindered Us, The Cool of the Day, The Fire Shall Be Ever Burning on the Altar, The Lot is Cast, Hitherto Hath the Lord Helped Us, They Did Eat of the Fruit of Canaan, Serve the Lord with Gladness, Do As Thou Hast Said, Oh That I Knew Where I might Find Him, He Shall Gather the Lambs with His Arms, He Began to Wash the Disciples Feet. Too many favorite quotes for me to produce them all here. Just read the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="574820304071375935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1245714885?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/41857272-kevin">Kevin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1245714885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15045434307559140768">I bought this version for my wife since english is her second language. Spurgeon's original words are obviously to be preferred over "updated" versions when possible, but this was most readable for her. We haven't actually read the entire year of devotions, but we've read a lot of them. Spurgeon's words are encouraging and speak powerfully into the life of the believer. He lived up to the title "Prince of Preacher", and that shines through in his writing! Though I must admit, his exegesis of the</span>
  <span id="freeText15045434307559140768" style="display:none">I bought this version for my wife since english is her second language. Spurgeon's original words are obviously to be preferred over "updated" versions when possible, but this was most readable for her. We haven't actually read the entire year of devotions, but we've read a lot of them. Spurgeon's words are encouraging and speak powerfully into the life of the believer. He lived up to the title "Prince of Preacher", and that shines through in his writing! Though I must admit, his exegesis of the text can be difficult to follow and from time to time rather baffling. Though, since he was a much more gifted theologian and preacher than I could ever hope to be, I'll chalk it up to my ignorance rather than has capability. Warmly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15045434307559140768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960968553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7549559672761283810">This book is a treasure. Over the past year plus, it has become precious to me. For most of the time that I have been reading it, I didn’t allow myself to underline or highlight anything, because it didn’t take long for me to understand that I would be highlighting and underlining a majority of the text. I have shared so many quotes with so many people, and even bought the book for several friends. I find myself saying “Spurgeon said…” more often than I am comfortable quoting any single man, and</span>
  <span id="freeText7549559672761283810" style="display:none">This book is a treasure. Over the past year plus, it has become precious to me. For most of the time that I have been reading it, I didn’t allow myself to underline or highlight anything, because it didn’t take long for me to understand that I would be highlighting and underlining a majority of the text. I have shared so many quotes with so many people, and even bought the book for several friends. I find myself saying “Spurgeon said…” more often than I am comfortable quoting any single man, and yet, as I recently told a friend, It isn’t Spurgeon himself—it’s that he was able to use truth, language, and emotion in such a way that it spurs me to become ever more excited about God, and to appreciate His majesty, His greatness, His faithfulness, and His goodness in a greater and greater ways. It’s not that Spurgeon is great (although he is a great writer!); it’s that he has a gift for pointing to the God who truly is great in every sense of the word. <br />This book is a keepsake. If you haven’t read it, do yourself a favor and buy a copy. You’ll be glad you did.<br /></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3386746544?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/1709540-debbie">Debbie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/43431445-morning-and-evening">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=devotional">devotional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3386746544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5542961877558755562">"Morning and Evening" is a year-long devotional with a devotion provided for both the morning and the evening of each day. The wording has been updated so that the English is easy to understand. Each devotion started with a verse from the Bible and then had Spurgeon's comments on it or on a related topic. I found a few of the devotions to be insightful, some were interesting, and some seemed to be more of historical interest (as none of the churches I've attended have quite so literally interpre</span>
  <span id="freeText5542961877558755562" style="display:none">"Morning and Evening" is a year-long devotional with a devotion provided for both the morning and the evening of each day. The wording has been updated so that the English is easy to understand. Each devotion started with a verse from the Bible and then had Spurgeon's comments on it or on a related topic. I found a few of the devotions to be insightful, some were interesting, and some seemed to be more of historical interest (as none of the churches I've attended have quite so literally interpreted the Song of Solomon as between the church and God). The devotions were short, so it didn't take long to read (or listen to, in this case, as it was an audiobook) each devotion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5542961877558755562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_667928258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667928258" />
    <a title="Linda " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1367242-linda"><img alt="Linda " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550467698p2/1367242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/667928258?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda " href="/user/show/1367242-linda">Linda </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780943575537" href="/book/show/1497293.Morning_and_Evening_King_James_Version">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1367242-linda?shelf=books-every-christian-should-read">books-every-christian-should-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1367242-linda?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1367242-linda?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1367242-linda?shelf=devotional">devotional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer667928258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15976361967285680098">Charles Haddon Spurgeon was an English preacher who lived from 1834-1892 and is known for his bold sermons and writings. At our church, we almost think of Spurgeon as an honorary elder because our pastors and teachers value and draw from his works so much. I've had the intention of reading a major work by Spurgeon for years and finally decided this year to go through his Morning and Evening devotionals, and I am finding it a tremendous blessing.<br/><br/>This volume is a collection of short devotionals - </span>
  <span id="freeText15976361967285680098" style="display:none">Charles Haddon Spurgeon was an English preacher who lived from 1834-1892 and is known for his bold sermons and writings. At our church, we almost think of Spurgeon as an honorary elder because our pastors and teachers value and draw from his works so much. I've had the intention of reading a major work by Spurgeon for years and finally decided this year to go through his Morning and Evening devotionals, and I am finding it a tremendous blessing.<br /><br />This volume is a collection of short devotionals - mini sermons really - two for each day of the year. Each one is based on one phrase or verse from Scripture and takes only about two minutes to read. It's amazing to me how much depth and meaning Spurgeon could get out of one short sentence! He then uses the context of the verse, other scriptures, and memorable illustrations and metaphors to expound the text and make application to the reader. Topics he touches on include: heaven, sin, judgment, suffering, prayer, God's Word, God's attributes, the atonement (Christ's work on the cross), the work of the Holy Spirit, the church, sanctification (the process of becoming holy), obedience and mortification of sin, and more.<br /><br />The selections provide the reader with a balanced variety of words of comfort and encouragement, reminders of spiritual truths, instruction and exhortation, and conviction. Here is just a small sampling of the "jewels" this volume contains:<br /><br />"God's altar was to be built of unhewn stones, that no trace of human skill or labour might be seen upon it... The proud heart of man is very anxious to have a hand in the justification of the soul before God... It were well if sinners would remember that so far from perfecting the Saviour's work, their carnal confidences only pollute and dishonour it."<br /><br />"It is a delightful and profitable occupation to mark the hand of God in the lives of ancient saints, and to observe His goodness in delivering them, His mercy in pardoning them, and His faithfulness in keeping His covenant with them. But ought we not to look upon our own history as being at least as full of God...as the lives of any of the saints who have gone before? We do our Lord an injustice when we suppose that He wrought all His mighty acts and showed Himself strong for those in the early time, but doth not perform wonders or lay bare his arm for the saints who are now upon the earth."<br /><br />"It is our duty and our privilege to wait upon the Lord in service, in worship, in expectancy, in trust all the days of our life. Our faith will be tried faith, and if it be of the true kind, it will bear continued trial without yielding. We shall not grow weary of waiting upon God if we remember how long and how graciously He once waited for us."<br /><br />"A prayerless soul is a Christless soul. Prayer is the lisping of the believing infant, the shout of the fighting believer, the requiem of the dying saint falling asleep in Jesus. It is the breath, the watchword, the comfort, the strength, the honour of a Christian. If thou be a child of God, thou wilt seek thy Father's face and live in thy Father's love."<br /><br />These daily readings will cause the reader to reflect on his own relationship and walk with God, to praise Him for His works, attributes, and promises, and at times to deal honestly with his heart and humble himself in repentance. The passages help the believer to take his eyes off himself - his merits, failings, and troubles - and to look instead to Christ. Sometimes the writer addresses that reader who may yet be in a state of unbelief to turn to Jesus, "to believe and live." Spurgeon's thoughts come from the heart of one who clearly loved and cared about people, but who loved his Lord above all else</span>
  <a data-text-id="15976361967285680098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_140565015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140565015" />
    <a title="Fylvia Kline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4793950-fylvia-kline"><img alt="Fylvia Kline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321721635p2/4793950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140565015?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fylvia Kline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fylvia Kline" href="/user/show/4793950-fylvia-kline">Fylvia Kline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780892217007" href="/book/show/9250621-mornings-and-evenings-with-spurgeon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140565015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16466901045967821075">This is an edited version of Spurgeon’s devotions from the 1800′s. A classic loved by scholars and laymen, it’s one of those devotions that can be used over and over again. And how you use it depends on how much personal devotion time you have carved out of the day for yourself.<br/><br/>To get the full Spurgeon effect, your dose for the day would be reading a page-long devotion in the morning, another one in the evening, memorizing one Bible text, and reading a significant portion of the Bible (towards t</span>
  <span id="freeText16466901045967821075" style="display:none">This is an edited version of Spurgeon’s devotions from the 1800′s. A classic loved by scholars and laymen, it’s one of those devotions that can be used over and over again. And how you use it depends on how much personal devotion time you have carved out of the day for yourself.<br /><br />To get the full Spurgeon effect, your dose for the day would be reading a page-long devotion in the morning, another one in the evening, memorizing one Bible text, and reading a significant portion of the Bible (towards the goal of reading the entire Bible in a year). All this is clearly laid out on two facing pages and makes it easy to navigate and pace yourself from January 1 to December 31. That’s a lot of reading and devotion time for the average person.<br /><br />If you are already in the habit of spending half hour alone with God at the beginning and end of each day, this is just the book for you. but if you just want a quick pick-me-up with your morning cup of coffee or a pinch of devotion at the long traffic light on your way to work, this is not for you. By that I mean, it’s not for you to use every morning and evening with regularity; but you can always use a reading whenever you want to be recharged with God’s Word. Just because these devotions are long and heavy is no reason to disregard them altogether.<br /><br />If you’re the kind that writes notes during your personal devotion, there’s ample white space around every reading. But, the pages are so Bible-thin that you can only use a pencil or one of those special pens that don’t bleed through. My first reaction to the paper was that the booked screamed “cheap,” but then I realized that two full-page devotions for a full year equals 730 pages which would result in a thick, hard-covered book that’s not very portable. So I can see why New Leaf went with thin pages and a paperback cover. It’s a practical choice.<br /><br />All in all, a great devotional. But I won’t be starting it until next year–I got it well into the new year and I’m not about to try to catch up a with 12 days of Spurgeon!<br /><br />(I received this book free from New Leaf Publishing Group. I was not required to write a positive review. The opinions I have expressed are my own.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16466901045967821075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_68128964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68128964" />
    <a title="Laurel Hicks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1719730-laurel-hicks"><img alt="Laurel Hicks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432779249p2/1719730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68128964?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel Hicks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel Hicks" href="/user/show/1719730-laurel-hicks">Laurel Hicks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Leather Bound 9781857921267" href="/book/show/6097640-morning-and-evening---burgundy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1719730-laurel-hicks?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1719730-laurel-hicks?shelf=0-kindle">0-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1719730-laurel-hicks?shelf=books-read-in-2009">books-read-in-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68128964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8617569838457277306">This book isn't for everybody, but if you've read quite a bit of the Bible and like beautiful language and thoughts, you might give it a try. Here is the morning reading for December 29 as a sample:<br/><br/>“Hitherto hath the Lord helped us.”<br/>1 Samuel 7:12<br/><br/>The word “hitherto” seems like a hand pointing in the direction of the past. Twenty years or seventy, and yet, “hitherto the Lord hath helped!” Through poverty, through wealth, through sickness, through health, at home, abroad, on the land, on the sea, i</span>
  <span id="freeText8617569838457277306" style="display:none">This book isn't for everybody, but if you've read quite a bit of the Bible and like beautiful language and thoughts, you might give it a try. Here is the morning reading for December 29 as a sample:<br /><br />“Hitherto hath the Lord helped us.”<br />1 Samuel 7:12<br /><br />The word “hitherto” seems like a hand pointing in the direction of the past. Twenty years or seventy, and yet, “hitherto the Lord hath helped!” Through poverty, through wealth, through sickness, through health, at home, abroad, on the land, on the sea, in honour, in dishonour, in perplexity, in joy, in trial, in triumph, in prayer, in temptation, “hitherto hath the Lord helped us!” We delight to look down a long avenue of trees. It is delightful to gaze from end to end of the long vista, a sort of verdant temple, with its branching pillars and its arches of leaves; even so look down the long aisles of your years, at the green boughs of mercy overhead, and the strong pillars of lovingkindness and faithfulness which bear up your joys. Are there no birds in yonder branches singing? Surely there must be many, and they all sing of mercy received “hitherto.”<br /><br />But the word also points forward. For when a man gets up to a certain mark and writes “hitherto,” he is not yet at the end, there is still a distance to be traversed. More trials, more joys; more temptations, more triumphs; more prayers, more answers; more toils, more strength; more fights, more victories; and then come sickness, old age, disease, death. Is it over now? No! there is more yet-awakening in Jesus’ likeness, thrones, harps, songs, psalms, white raiment, the face of Jesus, the society of saints, the glory of God, the fulness of eternity, the infinity of bliss. O be of good courage, believer, and with grateful confidence raise thy “Ebenezer,” for—<br /><br />He who hath helped thee hitherto<br /><br />Will help thee all thy journey through.<br /><br />When read in heaven’s light how glorious and marvellous a prospect will thy “hitherto” unfold to thy grateful eye!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8617569838457277306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9059633709986679023" style="display:none"> This book is like time travel with a really great Doctor for the soul. I think this old book I have, much older looking than the 1960 copywriter date came from a Library sale-- a bit of Avalon on earth for book lovers. It has old paper, old font, old words, even the verses are in put in Roman numerals. This book truly saved my life when I really needed it. I felt like I had a friend to speak into my life twice a day. Someone whose vague scripture references I usually got because I'm such a Bible geek. Someone who wasn't too simple, didactic or shallow. Someone who actually had something to say that was encouraging and inspiring. I'm glad this book has been translated into modern English. But I really love this old English. I wish someone would republish this in super contemporary language-- well I wish I could. I also wish someone would republish this with his biography interspersed with the dates it was written. That would be incredible. </span>

<div id="review_194520922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194520922" />
    <a title="Shannon Cooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5962088-shannon-cooper"><img alt="Shannon Cooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322760448p2/5962088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194520922?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon Cooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon Cooper" href="/user/show/5962088-shannon-cooper">Shannon Cooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194520922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1075854976407070318">I did enjoy this book of daily devotions by Spurgeon, but after reading this I find reading an entire sermon more helpful than little tidbits. Part of the problem could be that I read Morning and Evening like a regular book, rather than day by day. If you're able to discipline yourself in reading it like a devotional than I would suggest getting this book, otherwise I would recommend getting the collection of Spurgeon sermons.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_708040789" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/708040789" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23128494-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/708040789?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/23128494-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer708040789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14791934679494694104">This is a great devotional that challenges you and helps you grow in your walk with the Lord. The only thing that I did not like about these devotionals is that Spurgeon believes Song of Solomon is just a picture of Christ and the church and that it is not about the relationship between a man and a wife. There are multiple devotionals where he spiritualizes that book when he should not. Other than that it was a wonderful devotional!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Tb1t+D6jAfUGsHwRj85t5luTPVPPOhaD29QKs8nZtwzxto0/80pM1lxTokpg1WfVLe6uzlertT30xigM09ESaw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('++CJ4mTVj9+NyHxlc+SeKIzbttvIsUtUinrBPt1s+gVH62klqTzC/Ncroj6c/5Qb+qYlRlAg6OqlaOOBx2RfYg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2876959.Charles_Haddon_Spurgeon">About Charles Haddon Spurgeon</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2876959.Charles_Haddon_Spurgeon"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1283124007p3/2876959.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16167947176839893975">Charles Haddon Spurgeon (1834-92) was England's best-known preacher for most of the second half of the nineteenth century. In 1854, just four years after his conversion, Spurgeon, then only 20, became pastor of London's famed New Park Street Church (formerly pastored by the famous Baptist theologian John Gill). The congregation quickly outgrew their building, moved to Exeter Hall, then to Surrey M</span>
  <span id="freeText16167947176839893975" style="display:none">Charles Haddon Spurgeon (1834-92) was England's best-known preacher for most of the second half of the nineteenth century. In 1854, just four years after his conversion, Spurgeon, then only 20, became pastor of London's famed New Park Street Church (formerly pastored by the famous Baptist theologian John Gill). The congregation quickly outgrew their building, moved to Exeter Hall, then to Surrey Music Hall. In these venues Spurgeon frequently preached to audiences numbering more than 10,000—all in the days before electronic amplification. In 1861 the congregation moved permanently to the newly constructed Metropolitan Tabernacle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16167947176839893975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
